text-align:center">Ballpark\n</th></tr>\n<tr>\n<td colspan="2">\n<ul><li><a href="/wiki/Jarry_Park_Stadium" title="Jarry Park Stadium">Jarry Park Stadium</a> (1969\xe2\x80\x931976)</li>\n<li><a href="/wiki/Olympic_Stadium_(Montreal)" title="Olympic Stadium (Montreal)">Olympic Stadium</a> (1977\xe2\x80\x932004)</li>\n<li><a href="/wiki/Hiram_Bithorn_Stadium" title="Hiram Bithorn Stadium">Hiram Bithorn Stadium</a><sup>(1)</sup> (<a href="/wiki/San_Juan,_Puerto_Rico" title="San Juan, Puerto Rico">San Juan, Puerto Rico</a>) (2003\xe2\x80\x932004)</li></ul>\n<p><small>(1) \xe2\x80\x93 The Expos played twenty-two (of eighty-one) home games in San Juan during the 2003 and 2004 seasons respectively, and the remainder in Montreal.</small>\n</p>\n</td></tr>\n<tr>\n<th colspan="2" style="background-color:#dcdcdc; text-align:center">Team colours\n</th></tr>\n<tr>\n<td colspan="2">\n<ul><li><b>Blue</b>, <b>red</b>, <b>white</b></li></ul>\n<p><span style="background-color:#003087; color:white; border:1px solid #000000; text-align:center;">&#160;&#160;&#160;&#160;</span> <span style="background-color:#E4002B; color:white; border:1px solid #000000; text-align:center;">&#160;&#160;&#160;&#160;</span> <span style="background-color:#FFFFFF; color:black; border:1px solid #000000; text-align:center;">&#160;&#160;&#160;&#160;</span>\n</p>\n</td></tr>\n<tr>\n<th colspan="2" style="background-color:#dcdcdc; text-align:center">Major league titles\n</th></tr>\n<tr style="vertical-align:top">\n<td><b>World Series titles</b> (0)</td>\n<td width="135px">None\n</td></tr>\n<tr style="vertical-align:top">\n<td><b>NL pennants</b> (0)</td>\n<td width="135px">None\n</td></tr>\n<tr style="vertical-align:top">\n<td><b>East Division titles</b> (1)<sup>(2)(3)</sup></td>\n<td width="135px"><a href="/wiki/1981_Montreal_Expos_season" title="1981 Montreal Expos season">1981</a>\n</td></tr>\n<tr style="vertical-align: top">\n<td><b>Wild Card berths</b> (0)</td>\n<td width="135px">None\n</td></tr>\n<tr>\n<td colspan="2"><small>(2) \xe2\x80\x93 In <a href="/wiki/1981_in_baseball" title="1981 in baseball">1981</a>, a <a href="/wiki/1981_Major_League_Baseball_strike" title="1981 Major League Baseball strike">players\' strike</a> in the middle of the season forced the season to be split into two halves. Montreal won the division in the second half, despite having the second best record in the division when considering the entire season, two games behind <a href="/wiki/St._Louis_Cardinals" title="St. Louis Cardinals">St. Louis</a>.<br />\n</small><p><small>(3) \xe2\x80\x93 In <a href="/wiki/1994_in_baseball" title="1994 in baseball">1994</a>, a <a href="/wiki/1994%E2%80%9395_Major_League_Baseball_strike" title="1994\xe2\x80\x9395 Major League Baseball strike">players\' strike</a> wiped out the last eight weeks of the season and all post-season. Montreal was in first place by six games in the National League East Division when play was stopped. No official titles were awarded in 1994.</small>\n</p>\n</td></tr>\n<tr>\n<th colspan="2" style="background-color:#dcdcdc; text-align:center">Other team information\n</th></tr>\n<tr>\n<th>Retired numbers\n</th>\n<td><i><a href="/wiki/Gary_Carter" title="Gary Carter">8</a>, <a href="/wiki/Andre_Dawson" title="Andre Dawson">10</a>, <a href="/wiki/Rusty_Staub" title="Rusty Staub">10</a>, <a href="/wiki/Tim_Raines" title="Tim Raines">30</a>, <a href="/wiki/Jackie_Robinson" title="Jackie Robinson">42</a></i>\n</td></tr>\n<tr>\n<th>Mascot\n</th>\n<td>Souki (1978), <a href="/wiki/Youppi!" title="Youppi!">Youppi!</a> (1979\xe2\x80\x932004)<sup id="cite_ref-WashingtonPost-Youppi!_1-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-WashingtonPost-Youppi!-1">&#91;1&#93;</a></sup>\n</td></tr>\n<tr>\n<th>Theme Song\n</th>\n<td><i><i lang="fr" title="French language text">Les Expos sont l\xc3\xa0</i></i> ("The Expos are here") by Marc G\xc3\xa9linas\n</td></tr></tbody></table>\n<p>The <b>Montreal Expos</b> (French: <i lang="fr">Les Expos de Montr\xc3\xa9al</i>) were a Canadian <a href="/wiki/Professional_baseball" title="Professional baseball">professional baseball</a> team based in <a href="/wiki/Montreal" title="Montreal">Montreal, Quebec</a>. The Expos were the first <a href="/wiki/Major_League_Baseball" title="Major League Baseball">Major League Baseball</a> (MLB) franchise located outside the United States. They played in the <a href="/wiki/National_League" title="National League">National League</a> (NL) <a href="/wiki/National_League_East" title="National League East">East Division</a> from <a href="/wiki/1969_Montreal_Expos_season" title="1969 Montreal Expos season">1969</a> until <a href="/wiki/2004_Montreal_Expos_season" title="2004 Montreal Expos season">2004</a>. Following the 2004 season, the franchise <a href="/wiki/Relocation_of_professional_sports_teams" title="Relocation of professional sports teams">relocated</a> to Washington, D.C., and became the <a href="/wiki/Washington_Nationals" title="Washington Nationals">Washington Nationals</a>.\n</p><p>Immediately after the <a href="/wiki/Minor_League_Baseball" title="Minor League Baseball">minor league</a> <a href="/wiki/Triple-A_(baseball)" title="Triple-A (baseball)">Triple-A</a> <a href="/wiki/Montreal_Royals" title="Montreal Royals">Montreal Royals</a> folded in 1960, political leaders in Montreal sought an MLB franchise, and when the <a href="/wiki/National_League" title="National League">National League</a> evaluated <a href="/wiki/1969_Major_League_Baseball_expansion" title="1969 Major League Baseball expansion">expansion candidates for the 1969 season</a>, it awarded a team to Montreal. Named after the <a href="/wiki/Expo_67" title="Expo 67">Expo 67</a> <a href="/wiki/World%27s_Fair" class="mw-redirect" title="World&#39;s Fair">World\'s Fair</a>, the Expos originally played at <a href="/wiki/Jarry_Park_Stadium" title="Jarry Park Stadium">Jarry Park Stadium</a> before moving to <a href="/wiki/Olympic_Stadium_(Montreal)" title="Olympic Stadium (Montreal)">Olympic Stadium</a> in 1977. The Expos failed to post a winning record in any of their first ten seasons. The team won its only division title in the <a href="/wiki/1981_Major_League_Baseball_strike" title="1981 Major League Baseball strike">strike-shortened</a> <a href="/wiki/1981_Major_League_Baseball_season" title="1981 Major League Baseball season">1981</a> season, but lost the <a href="/wiki/1981_National_League_Championship_Series" title="1981 National League Championship Series">1981 National League Championship Series</a> (NLCS) to the <a href="/wiki/Los_Angeles_Dodgers" title="Los Angeles Dodgers">Los Angeles Dodgers</a>. The team was sold in 1991 by its majority, founding owner, <a href="/wiki/Charles_Bronfman" title="Charles Bronfman">Charles Bronfman</a>, to a consortium headed by <a href="/wiki/Claude_Brochu" title="Claude Brochu">Claude Brochu</a>. <a href="/wiki/Felipe_Alou" title="Felipe Alou">Felipe Alou</a> was promoted to the team\'s field manager in 1992, becoming MLB\'s first Dominican-born manager. He led the team to four winning seasons, including <a href="/wiki/1994_Major_League_Baseball_season" title="1994 Major League Baseball season">1994</a>, where the Expos had the best record in baseball before a <a href="/wiki/1994%E2%80%9395_Major_League_Baseball_strike" title="1994\xe2\x80\x9395 Major League Baseball strike">players\' strike</a> ended the season. Alou became the Expos leader in games managed (1409).\n</p><p>The aftermath of the 1994 strike initiated a downward spiral as the Expos chose to sell off their best players, and attendance and interest in the team declined. Major League Baseball purchased the team prior to the 2002 season after the club failed to secure funding for a new ballpark. In their final two seasons, the team played 22 home games each year at <a href="/wiki/Hiram_Bithorn_Stadium" title="Hiram Bithorn Stadium">Hiram Bithorn Stadium</a> in <a href="/wiki/San_Juan,_Puerto_Rico" title="San Juan, Puerto Rico">San Juan, Puerto Rico</a>. On September 29, 2004, MLB announced the franchise would relocate to Washington, D.C. for the <a href="/wiki/2005_Major_League_Baseball_season" title="2005 Major League Baseball season">2005</a> season,<sup id="cite_ref-MLBSelectsDCForExpos_2-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-MLBSelectsDCForExpos-2">&#91;2&#93;</a></sup> and the Expos played their final home game in Montreal.\n</p><p>The Expos posted an all-time record of 2,753 wins, 2,943 losses and 4 ties during their 36 years in Montreal. <a href="/wiki/Vladimir_Guerrero" title="Vladimir Guerrero">Vladimir Guerrero</a> led the franchise in both <a href="/wiki/Home_run" title="Home run">home runs</a> and <a href="/wiki/Batting_average" title="Batting average">batting average</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Steve_Rogers_(baseball)" title="Steve Rogers (baseball)">Steve Rogers</a> in <a href="/wiki/Win_(baseball)" class="mw-redirect" title="Win (baseball)">wins</a> and <a href="/wiki/Strikeout" title="Strikeout">strikeouts</a>. Three pitchers threw four <a href="/wiki/No-hitter" title="No-hitter">no-hitters</a>: <a href="/wiki/Bill_Stoneman" title="Bill Stoneman">Bill Stoneman</a> (twice), <a href="/wiki/Charlie_Lea" title="Charlie Lea">Charlie Lea</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Dennis_Mart%C3%ADnez" title="Dennis Mart\xc3\xadnez">Dennis Mart\xc3\xadnez</a>, who pitched the <a href="/wiki/Dennis_Mart%C3%ADnez%27s_perfect_game" title="Dennis Mart\xc3\xadnez&#39;s perfect game">13th official perfect game</a> in Major League Baseball history. The Expos retired four numbers in Montreal, and nine former members have been elected to the <a href="/wiki/National_Baseball_Hall_of_Fame" class="mw-redirect" title="National Baseball Hall of Fame">National Baseball Hall of Fame</a>, with <a href="/wiki/Gary_Carter" title="Gary Carter">Gary Carter</a>, <a href="/wiki/Andre_Dawson" title="Andre Dawson">Andre Dawson</a> and <a href="/wiki/Tim_Raines" title="Tim Raines">Tim Raines</a>\' plaques depicting them with Expos caps.\n</p>\n<div id="toc" class="toc"><input type="checkbox" role="button" id="toctogglecheckbox" class="toctogglecheckbox" style="display:none" /><div class="toctitle" lang="en" dir="ltr"><h2>Contents</h2><span class="toctogglespan"><label class="toctogglelabel" for="toctogglecheckbox"></label></span></div>\n<ul>\n<li class="toclevel-1 tocsection-1"><a href="#History"><span class="tocnumber">1</span> <span class="toctext">History</span></a>\n<ul>\n<li class="toclevel-2 tocsection-2"><a href="#Founding_(1960\xe2\x80\x931968)"><span class="tocnumber">1.1</span> <span class="toctext">Founding (1960\xe2\x80\x931968)</span></a></li>\n<li class="toclevel-2 tocsection-3"><a href="#Jarry_Park_years_(1969\xe2\x80\x931976)"><span class="tocnumber">1.2</span> <span class="toctext">Jarry Park years (1969\xe2\x80\x931976)</span></a></li>\n<li class="toclevel-2 tocsection-4"><a href="#The_Big_O_and_Blue_Monday_(1977\xe2\x80\x931981)"><span class="tocnumber">1.3</span> <span class="toctext">The Big O and Blue Monday (1977\xe2\x80\x931981)</span></a></li>\n<li class="toclevel-2 tocsection-5"><a href="#&quot;The_team_of_the_&#39;80s&quot;_(1982\xe2\x80\x931988)"><span class="tocnumber">1.4</span> <span class="toctext">"The team of the \'80s" (1982\xe2\x80\x931988)</span></a></li>\n<li class="toclevel-2 tocsection-6"><a href="#&quot;El_Presidente,_El_Perfecto!&quot;_(1989\xe2\x80\x931993)"><span class="tocnumber">1.5</span> <span class="toctext">"El Presidente, El Perfecto!" (2001\xe2\x80\x932004)</span></a></li>\n</ul>\n</li>\n<li class="toclevel-1 tocsection-10"><a href="#Team_identity"><span class="tocnumber">2</span> <span class="toctext">Team identity</span></a>\n<ul>\n<li class="toclevel-2 tocsection-11"><a href="#Youppi!"><span class="tocnumber">2.1</span> <span class="toctext">Youppi!</span></a></li>\n</ul>\n</li>\n<li class="toclevel-1 tocsection-12"><a href="#Relationship_with_the_Toronto_Blue_Jays"><span class="tocnumber">3</span> <span class="toctext">Relationship with the Toronto Blue Jays</span></a></li>\n<li class="toclevel-1 tocsection-13"><a href="#Players"><span class="tocnumber">4</span> <span class="toctext">Players</span></a>\n<ul>\n<li class="toclevel-2 tocsection-14"><a href="#Retired_numbers"><span class="tocnumber">4.1</span> <span class="toctext">Retired numbers</span></a></li>\n<li class="toclevel-2 tocsection-15"><a href="#National_Baseball_Hall_of_Fame"><span class="tocnumber">4.2</span> <span class="toctext">National Baseball Hall of Fame</span></a></li>\n<li class="toclevel-2 tocsection-16"><a href="#Montreal_Expos_Hall_of_Fame"><span class="tocnumber">4.3</span> <span class="toctext">Montreal Expos Hall of Fame</span></a></li>\n</ul>\n</li>\n<li class="toclevel-1 tocsection-17"><a href="#Expos_records"><span class="tocnumber">5</span> <span class="toctext">Expos records</span></a></li>\n<li class="toclevel-1 tocsection-18"><a href="#No-hitters_and_cycles"><span class="tocnumber">6</span> <span class="toctext">No-hitters and cycles</span></a></li>\n<li class="toclevel-1 tocsection-19"><a href="#See_also"><span class="tocnumber">7</span> <span class="toctext">See also</span></a></li>\n<li class="toclevel-1 tocsection-20"><a href="#References"><span class="tocnumber">8</span> <span class="toctext">References</span></a>\n<ul>\n<li class="toclevel-2 tocsection-21"><a href="#Footnotes"><span class="tocnumber">8.1</span> <span class="toctext">Footnotes</span></a></li>\n<li class="toclevel-2 tocsection-22"><a href="#General"><span class="tocnumber">8.2</span> <span class="toctext">General</span></a></li>\n</ul>\n</li>\n<li class="toclevel-1 tocsection-23"><a href="#External_links"><span class="tocnumber">9</span> <span class="toctext">External links</span></a></li>\n</ul>\n</div>\n\n<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="History">History</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Montreal_Expos&amp;action=edit&amp;section=1" title="Edit section: History">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>\n<h3><span id="Founding_.281960.E2.80.931968.29"></span><span class="mw-headline" id="Founding_(1960\xe2\x80\x931968)">Founding (1960\xe2\x80\x931968)</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Montreal_Expos&amp;action=edit&amp;section=2" title="Edit section: Founding (1960\xe2\x80\x931968)">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<p>Professional baseball in Montreal dates back to 1890 when teams briefly played in the <a href="/wiki/International_League" title="International League">International Association</a>. A second attempt at hosting a pro team failed in 1895. The <a href="/wiki/Montreal_Royals" title="Montreal Royals">Montreal Royals</a> of the <a href="/wiki/Eastern_League_(baseball,_1884%E2%80%931912)" class="mw-redirect" title="Eastern League (baseball, 1884\xe2\x80\x931912)">Eastern League</a> were subsequently founded in 1897 and played 20 seasons.<sup id="cite_ref-3" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-3">&#91;3&#93;</a></sup> The Royals were revived in 1928 and were purchased by the <a href="/wiki/Brooklyn_Dodgers" class="mw-redirect" title="Brooklyn Dodgers">Brooklyn Dodgers</a> in 1939 to serve as one of their <a href="/wiki/Triple-A_(baseball)" title="Triple-A (baseball)">Triple-A</a> affiliates.<sup id="cite_ref-4" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-4">&#91;4&#93;</a></sup> Under Dodgers\' management, the Royals won seven International League championships and three <a href="/wiki/Junior_World_Series" title="Junior World Series">Junior World Series</a> titles between 1941 and 1958.<sup id="cite_ref-5" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-5">&#91;5&#93;</a></sup> In 1946, <a href="/wiki/Jackie_Robinson" title="Jackie Robinson">Jackie Robinson</a> joined the Royals and led the team to a Junior World Series title in advance of his breaking baseball\'s <a href="/wiki/Baseball_color_line" title="Baseball color line">colour barrier</a> one year later.<sup id="cite_ref-6" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-6">&#91;6&#93;</a></sup> By the late 1950s, the Royals\' championship years were past, and faced with declining attendance, the team was sold and relocated following the 1960 season as the Dodgers reduced the number of teams they maintained at the AAA level.<sup id="cite_ref-Keri5_7-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Keri5-7">&#91;7&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>Almost immediately upon the Royals\' demise, Montreal mayor <a href="/wiki/Jean_Drapeau" title="Jean Drapeau">Jean Drapeau</a> and city executive committee chairman Gerry Snyder began their campaign for a <a href="/wiki/Major_League_Baseball" title="Major League Baseball">Major League Baseball</a> (MLB) team.<sup id="cite_ref-Keri5_7-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Keri5-7">&#91;7&#93;</a></sup>  The city, which had previously been considered a leading candidate to acquire the <a href="/wiki/St._Louis_Browns" class="mw-redirect" title="St. Louis Browns">St. Louis Browns</a> if the team had relocated in 1933,<sup id="cite_ref-8" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-8">&#91;8&#93;</a></sup> was too late to submit its candidacy for a team as part of the <a href="/wiki/National_League" title="National League">National League</a>\'s (NL) 1962 expansion but presented its bid to the league\'s owners at the winter meetings in 1967.<sup id="cite_ref-9" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-9">&#91;9&#93;</a></sup> Aiding Montreal\'s bid was the fact that <a href="/wiki/Walter_O%27Malley" title="Walter O&#39;Malley">Walter O\'Malley</a>, who owned the Dodgers and formerly oversaw the Montreal Royals, was the chairman of the NL\'s expansion committee.<sup id="cite_ref-Keri7_10-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Keri7-10">&#91;10&#93;</a></sup> On May 27, 1968, National League president <a href="/wiki/Warren_Giles" title="Warren Giles">Warren Giles</a> announced the league would add expansion teams in <a href="/wiki/San_Diego_Padres" title="San Diego Padres">San Diego</a> and Montreal at a cost of US$10 million each.<sup id="cite_ref-MGExpansion_11-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-MGExpansion-11">&#91;11&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>With the franchise secured, Snyder built an ownership group of six partners led by financier <a href="/wiki/Jean-Louis_L%C3%A9vesque" title="Jean-Louis L\xc3\xa9vesque">Jean-Louis L\xc3\xa9vesque</a> and <a href="/wiki/Seagram" title="Seagram">Seagram</a> heir <a href="/wiki/Charles_Bronfman" title="Charles Bronfman">Charles Bronfman</a>.  L\xc3\xa9vesque was originally tapped as chairman and the public face of the ownership group since he was a francophone. However, he bowed out, and Bronfman took over as chairman.<sup id="cite_ref-12" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-12">&#91;12&#93;</a></sup> The new group was faced with the immediate problem of finding a suitable facility in which to play for at least two years.<sup id="cite_ref-13" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-13">&#91;13&#93;</a></sup> Drapeau had promised the NL that a domed stadium would be built by 1971.<sup id="cite_ref-MGExpansion_11-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-MGExpansion-11">&#91;11&#93;</a></sup> However, Snyder\'s successor as executive committee chairman, <a href="/wiki/Lucien_Saulnier" title="Lucien Saulnier">Lucien Saulnier</a>, told Bronfman that Drapeau could not make such a guarantee on his own authority.  As 1968 dragged on without movement from the city on a facility, Bronfman and his group threatened to walk away. While they had more than enough money between them to pay the first installment of the expansion fee, they wanted assurances that a park would be built before proceeding any further with the effort.<sup id="cite_ref-14" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-14">&#91;14&#93;</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Delorimier_Stadium" title="Delorimier Stadium">Delorimier Stadium</a>, which hosted the Royals, was rejected even as a temporary facility; it could not be expanded beyond its 20,000-seat capacity because it was in a residential area.  The <a href="/wiki/Autostade" title="Autostade">Autostade</a>, home of the <a href="/wiki/Canadian_Football_League" title="Canadian Football League">Canadian Football League</a>\'s <a href="/wiki/Montreal_Alouettes" title="Montreal Alouettes">Montreal Alouettes</a>, was ruled out due to the prohibitive cost of expanding it and adding a dome,<sup id="cite_ref-15" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-15">&#91;15&#93;</a></sup> as well as doubts that the city even had the right to make the needed renovations to the federally-owned facility.<sup id="cite_ref-GazetteJarry_16-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-GazetteJarry-16">&#91;16&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>By August 1968, the NL owners had grown increasingly concerned about the unresolved stadium question, putting the franchise\'s future in doubt. There were rumours of awarding the franchise to <a href="/wiki/Buffalo,_New_York" title="Buffalo, New York">Buffalo, New York</a> instead, whose <a href="/wiki/War_Memorial_Stadium_(Buffalo)" class="mw-redirect" title="War Memorial Stadium (Buffalo)">War Memorial Stadium</a> was ready to host a team.<sup id="cite_ref-17" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-17">&#91;17&#93;</a></sup> League president <a href="/wiki/Warren_Giles" title="Warren Giles">Warren Giles</a> was reassured of Montreal\'s viability when shown a 3,000-seat community field in the centrally located <a href="/wiki/Jarry_Park" title="Jarry Park">Jarry Park</a> that Drapeau proposed expanding to 30,000 seats as a temporary home for the Expos, at a cost of over C$1 million.<sup id="cite_ref-GazetteJarry_16-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-GazetteJarry-16">&#91;16&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>Several options for a team name were considered: "Royals" was a popular option with fans, but the name had already been taken by the <a href="/wiki/Kansas_City_Royals" title="Kansas City Royals">Kansas City Royals</a>. Other names considered included "Voyageurs" and "Nationals".<sup id="cite_ref-Keri15_18-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Keri15-18">&#91;18&#93;</a></sup> The team settled on "Expos", a name with the same spelling in French and English, in recognition of the recently concluded <a href="/wiki/Expo_67" title="Expo 67">Expo 67</a> <a href="/wiki/World%27s_Fair" class="mw-redirect" title="World&#39;s Fair">World\'s Fair</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-Keri15_18-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Keri15-18">&#91;18&#93;</a></sup> Less than a year after the city was awarded a team, the Expos took to the field to begin the <a href="/wiki/1969_Major_League_Baseball_season" title="1969 Major League Baseball season">1969</a> season.<sup id="cite_ref-19" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-19">&#91;19&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h3><span id="Jarry_Park_years_.281969.E2.80.931976.29"></span><span class="mw-headline" id="Jarry_Park_years_(1969\xe2\x80\x931976)">Jarry Park years (1969\xe2\x80\x931976)</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Montreal_Expos&amp;action=edit&amp;section=3" title="Edit section: Jarry Park years (1969\xe2\x80\x931976)">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Jarry_night.jpg" class="image"><img alt="Fans watch a game from the third base line; the scoreboard is visible beyond the right field wall." src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/1c/Jarry_night.jpg/220px-Jarry_night.jpg" width="220" height="206" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/1c/Jarry_night.jpg/330px-Jarry_night.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/1c/Jarry_night.jpg/440px-Jarry_night.jpg 2x" data-file-width="844" data-file-height="789" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Jarry_night.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>A game at Jarry Park, 1969</div></div></div>\n<p>With <a href="/wiki/Gene_Mauch" title="Gene Mauch">Gene Mauch</a> as their inaugural manager, the Expos made their debut on April 8, 1969: an 11\xe2\x80\x9310 victory over the <a href="/wiki/New_York_Mets" title="New York Mets">New York Mets</a> at <a href="/wiki/Shea_Stadium" title="Shea Stadium">Shea Stadium</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-20" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-20">&#91;20&#93;</a></sup> The team played its first home game&#8212;and the first Major League game outside the United States&#8212;on April 14; it was an 8\xe2\x80\x937 victory over the <a href="/wiki/St._Louis_Cardinals" title="St. Louis Cardinals">St. Louis Cardinals</a> before 29,184 fans at <a href="/wiki/Jarry_Park_Stadium" title="Jarry Park Stadium">Jarry Park Stadium</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-21" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-21">&#91;21&#93;</a></sup> Three days later, on April 17, <a href="/wiki/Bill_Stoneman" title="Bill Stoneman">Bill Stoneman</a> pitched the first <a href="/wiki/No-hitter" title="No-hitter">no-hitter</a> in Expos history with a 7\xe2\x80\x930 victory over the <a href="/wiki/Philadelphia_Phillies" title="Philadelphia Phillies">Philadelphia Phillies</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-Stoneman1969NoHitter_22-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Stoneman1969NoHitter-22">&#91;22&#93;</a></sup> The excitement of the early-season heroics quickly gave way to the realities of being an expansion team as the Expos struggled for much of their inaugural season.<sup id="cite_ref-Keri25_23-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Keri25-23">&#91;23&#93;</a></sup> Montreal tied their expansion cousins, the <a href="/wiki/San_Diego_Padres" title="San Diego Padres">San Diego Padres</a> for the worst record in the NL with a record of 52\xe2\x80\x93110.<sup id="cite_ref-24" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-24">&#91;24&#93;</a></sup> The team fared little better in the following seasons; the Expos went 73\xe2\x80\x9389 in <a href="/wiki/1970_Major_League_Baseball_season" title="1970 Major League Baseball season">1970</a> and 71\xe2\x80\x9390 in <a href="/wiki/1971_Major_League_Baseball_season" title="1971 Major League Baseball season">1971</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-BRSeasonbySeason_25-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-BRSeasonbySeason-25">&#91;25&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>The team\'s best player, and first star, in its early seasons was <a href="/wiki/Rusty_Staub" title="Rusty Staub">Rusty Staub</a>. Acquired from the <a href="/wiki/Houston_Astros" title="Houston Astros">Houston Astros</a> in a trade prior to the Expos\' inaugural season,<sup id="cite_ref-Keri25_23-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Keri25-23">&#91;23&#93;</a></sup> he led the Expos with 30 home runs in 1970 and, owing to his red hair, was nicknamed <i>Le Grand Orange</i>.<sup id="cite_ref-Humber123_26-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Humber123-26">&#91;26&#93;</a></sup> Staub was Montreal\'s lone representative at the <a href="/wiki/Major_League_Baseball_All-Star_Game" title="Major League Baseball All-Star Game">Major League Baseball All-Star Game</a> in the team\'s first three seasons, and endeared himself to the local fans by learning French.<sup id="cite_ref-27" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-27">&#91;27&#93;</a></sup> Also popular was pitcher <a href="/wiki/Claude_Raymond_(baseball)" title="Claude Raymond (baseball)">Claude Raymond</a>, who completed his Major League career with Montreal in 1972 and was the team\'s first French-Canadian star.<sup id="cite_ref-Humber123_26-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Humber123-26">&#91;26&#93;</a></sup> Pitcher <a href="/wiki/Carl_Morton" title="Carl Morton">Carl Morton</a>, who posted an 18\xe2\x80\x9311 record in 1970, was the first player in franchise history to be named <a href="/wiki/Major_League_Baseball_Rookie_of_the_Year_Award" title="Major League Baseball Rookie of the Year Award">National League Rookie of the Year</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-28" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-28">&#91;28&#93;</a></sup> Bill Stoneman threw his second no-hitter, and the first pitched outside the United States, in a 7\xe2\x80\x930 win over the Mets in Montreal on October 2, 1972.<sup id="cite_ref-Stoneman1972NoHitter_29-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Stoneman1972NoHitter-29">&#91;29&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>The team failed to post a winning season in its first ten years and finished fifth or sixth in the six-team NL East eight times.<sup id="cite_ref-BRSeasonbySeason_25-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-BRSeasonbySeason-25">&#91;25&#93;</a></sup> Attendance declined as the initial excitement of having a team wore off.  It recovered briefly in <a href="/wiki/1973_Major_League_Baseball_season" title="1973 Major League Baseball season">1973</a> as the Expos mounted an unsuccessful charge at the NL East pennant, before declining sharply in <a href="/wiki/1974_Major_League_Baseball_season" title="1974 Major League Baseball season">1974</a> and beyond.<sup id="cite_ref-30" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-30">&#91;30&#93;</a></sup> By <a href="/wiki/1976_Major_League_Baseball_season" title="1976 Major League Baseball season">1976</a>, attendance had dropped to just over 600,000 fans over the course of the season, less than half of what the Expos drew in their inaugural season.<sup id="cite_ref-Humber123_26-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Humber123-26">&#91;26&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>The on-field product was not the only concern for the Expos.  Jarry Park was only intended to serve as a temporary home until 1971 at the latest.<sup id="cite_ref-SABROlympicStadium_31-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-SABROlympicStadium-31">&#91;31&#93;</a></sup>  Even allowing for this, it left much to be desired as a baseball venue.  The grandstands were completely exposed to the elements, forcing the Expos to postpone a number of early-season games.  Additionally, the sun set directly in the face of first basemen, forcing delays.  Due to numerous delays and cost overruns with its intended replacement, <a href="/wiki/Olympic_Stadium_(Montreal)" title="Olympic Stadium (Montreal)">Olympic Stadium</a>, the Expos were forced to stay in Jarry until 1976.<sup id="cite_ref-32" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-32">&#91;32&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>The team\'s future was also placed in doubt following an angry speech by Bronfman in which he threatened to relocate his family and the <a href="/wiki/Seagram" title="Seagram">Seagram</a> company outside Quebec if the separatist <a href="/wiki/Parti_Qu%C3%A9b%C3%A9cois" title="Parti Qu\xc3\xa9b\xc3\xa9cois">Parti Qu\xc3\xa9b\xc3\xa9cois</a> (PQ) won a majority government in the <a href="/wiki/Quebec_general_election,_1976" title="Quebec general election, 1976">1976 Quebec election</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-33" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-33">&#91;33&#93;</a></sup> The Parti Qu\xc3\xa9b\xc3\xa9cois did win the election; however, Bronfman and the Expos remained in Quebec.<sup id="cite_ref-34" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-34">&#91;34&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h3><span id="The_Big_O_and_Blue_Monday_.281977.E2.80.931981.29"></span><span class="mw-headline" id="The_Big_O_and_Blue_Monday_(1977\xe2\x80\x931981)">The Big O and Blue Monday (1977\xe2\x80\x931981)</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Montreal_Expos&amp;action=edit&amp;section=4" title="Edit section: The Big O and Blue Monday (1977\xe2\x80\x931981)">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<p>For the <a href="/wiki/1977_Major_League_Baseball_season" title="1977 Major League Baseball season">1977</a> season, the Expos moved into their new ballpark, <a href="/wiki/Olympic_Stadium_(Montreal)" title="Olympic Stadium (Montreal)">Olympic Stadium</a>, six years later than originally scheduled.<sup id="cite_ref-35" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-35">&#91;35&#93;</a></sup> For a time in the 1976\xe2\x80\x9377 offseason, however, it appeared that the Expos would have to play at least the early part of the season at Jarry Park due to delays in securing a lease for Olympic Stadium.  The team broke off negotiations not long after the PQ\'s landslide victory in the 1976 provincial election.  Negotiations dragged out through the winter, leading the Expos to begin selling 1977 season tickets under the assumption they would have to play at Jarry.  However, an agreement was finally reached in early 1977.<sup id="cite_ref-SABROlympicStadium_31-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-SABROlympicStadium-31">&#91;31&#93;</a></sup>  A total of 57,592 fans attended Montreal\'s <a href="/wiki/Opening_day" class="mw-redirect" title="Opening day">opening day</a> 7\xe2\x80\x932 loss to Philadelphia.<sup id="cite_ref-36" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-36">&#91;36&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>The new facility was a significant upgrade, although weather-related issues created by Montreal\'s harsh climate persisted until the stadium\'s roof was installed in 1987.  Over the years, the stadium became notorious for its poor playing conditions.  Players were frequently at risk for injury due to thin padding on the outfield fences, as well as the original <a href="/wiki/Artificial_turf" title="Artificial turf">artificial turf</a> that remained in place for over two decades. Ultimately, the park became viewed as a <a href="/wiki/White_elephant" title="White elephant">white elephant</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-37" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-37">&#91;37&#93;</a></sup> On the field, the Expos continued to fare poorly; the team won 75 games in 1977, and 76 in <a href="/wiki/1978_Major_League_Baseball_season" title="1978 Major League Baseball season">1978</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-BRSeasonbySeason_25-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-BRSeasonbySeason-25">&#91;25&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>Though the losing seasons mounted, the Expos built a solid core of players, led by <a href="/wiki/Gary_Carter" title="Gary Carter">Gary Carter</a>, who went on to become one of baseball\'s best hitting catchers,<sup id="cite_ref-38" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-38">&#91;38&#93;</a></sup> pitcher <a href="/wiki/Steve_Rogers_(baseball)" title="Steve Rogers (baseball)">Steve Rogers</a> and outfielders <a href="/wiki/Andre_Dawson" title="Andre Dawson">Andre Dawson</a> and <a href="/wiki/Tim_Raines" title="Tim Raines">Tim Raines</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-Humber123_26-3" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Humber123-26">&#91;26&#93;</a></sup> They supplemented their young roster with veteran acquisitions such as future <a href="/wiki/National_Baseball_Hall_of_Fame_and_Museum" title="National Baseball Hall of Fame and Museum">Hall of Famer</a> <a href="/wiki/Tony_P%C3%A9rez" title="Tony P\xc3\xa9rez">Tony P\xc3\xa9rez</a>,<sup id="cite_ref-39" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-39">&#91;39&#93;</a></sup> and in 1977, the Expos also hired <a href="/wiki/Dick_Williams" title="Dick Williams">Dick Williams</a> as the team\'s manager. Williams had developed a reputation for nurturing young talent; he had managed a young <a href="/wiki/Boston_Red_Sox" title="Boston Red Sox">Boston Red Sox</a> team to the American League pennant in <a href="/wiki/1967_Major_League_Baseball_season" title="1967 Major League Baseball season">1967</a> and the <a href="/wiki/Oakland_Athletics" title="Oakland Athletics">Oakland Athletics</a> to back-to-back <a href="/wiki/World_Series" title="World Series">World Series</a> titles in 1972 and 1973.<sup id="cite_ref-40" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-40">&#91;40&#93;</a></sup> In <a href="/wiki/1979_Major_League_Baseball_season" title="1979 Major League Baseball season">1979</a>, Montreal had its first winning season in franchise history; in mid-July, the Expos led the NL East by 6.5 games,<sup id="cite_ref-41" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-41">&#91;41&#93;</a></sup> before finishing second to the <a href="/wiki/Pittsburgh_Pirates" title="Pittsburgh Pirates">Pittsburgh Pirates</a> by two games with a 95\xe2\x80\x9365 record.<sup id="cite_ref-BRSeasonbySeason_25-3" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-BRSeasonbySeason-25">&#91;25&#93;</a></sup> The fans responded: Montreal drew two million fans for the first time in franchise history and it was the first of five consecutive seasons that the team was in the top-four of National League attendance.<sup id="cite_ref-42" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-42">&#91;42&#93;</a></sup> Though they won five fewer games in <a href="/wiki/1980_Major_League_Baseball_season" title="1980 Major League Baseball season">1980</a>, the Expos finished merely one game behind the Philadelphia Phillies for the division lead.<sup id="cite_ref-43" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-43">&#91;43&#93;</a></sup> In both seasons, the Expos were in the hunt for the division title into the last weekend of the season before losing to the ultimate World Series champion.<sup id="cite_ref-44" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-44">&#91;44&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<style data-mw-deduplicate="TemplateStyles:r856303569">@media all and (max-width:720px){.mw-parser-output .tmulti>.thumbinner{width:100%!important;max-width:none!important}.mw-parser-output .tmulti .tsingle{float:none!important;max-width:none!important;width:100%!important;text-align:center}}</style><div class="thumb tmulti tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:446px;max-width:446px"><div class="tsingle" style="float:left;margin:1px;width:252px;max-width:252px"><div class="thumbimage"><a href="/wiki/File:Montreal_Expos_baseball_cap_1969-1991.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d5/Montreal_Expos_baseball_cap_1969-1991.jpg/250px-Montreal_Expos_baseball_cap_1969-1991.jpg" width="250" height="188" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d5/Montreal_Expos_baseball_cap_1969-1991.jpg/375px-Montreal_Expos_baseball_cap_1969-1991.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d5/Montreal_Expos_baseball_cap_1969-1991.jpg/500px-Montreal_Expos_baseball_cap_1969-1991.jpg 2x" data-file-width="3456" data-file-height="2592" /></a></div></div><div class="tsingle" style="float:left;margin:1px;width:190px;max-width:190px"><div class="thumbimage"><a href="/wiki/File:Montreal_Expos_baseball_jersey_1969-1991.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/20/Montreal_Expos_baseball_jersey_1969-1991.jpg/188px-Montreal_Expos_baseball_jersey_1969-1991.jpg" width="188" height="188" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/20/Montreal_Expos_baseball_jersey_1969-1991.jpg/282px-Montreal_Expos_baseball_jersey_1969-1991.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/20/Montreal_Expos_baseball_jersey_1969-1991.jpg/376px-Montreal_Expos_baseball_jersey_1969-1991.jpg 2x" data-file-width="1920" data-file-height="1920" /></a></div></div><div style="clear:left"></div><div class="thumbcaption" style="clear:left;text-align:left;background-color:transparent">Baseball hat and home jersey worn by the Montreal Expos players from 1969 to 1991.</div></div></div>\n<p>In <a href="/wiki/1981_Major_League_Baseball_season" title="1981 Major League Baseball season">1981</a>, <a href="/wiki/Charlie_Lea" title="Charlie Lea">Charlie Lea</a> pitched the third no-hitter in franchise history. He defeated the <a href="/wiki/San_Francisco_Giants" title="San Francisco Giants">San Francisco Giants</a> by a 4\xe2\x80\x930 score on May 10, 1981.<sup id="cite_ref-LeaNoHitter_45-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-LeaNoHitter-45">&#91;45&#93;</a></sup> The Expos were in third place in the NL East with a 30\xe2\x80\x9325 record when the season was halted for two months by a <a href="/wiki/1981_Major_League_Baseball_strike" title="1981 Major League Baseball strike">players\' strike</a>. By the time the strike ended, 713 games had been lost and could not possibly be made up.  Major League Baseball chose to adopt a split-season schedule, which gave the Expos a fresh start in the second half of the season.<sup id="cite_ref-46" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-46">&#91;46&#93;</a></sup> With the team languishing near the .500 mark in post-strike play, the club fired Williams and replaced him with scouting director <a href="/wiki/Jim_Fanning" title="Jim Fanning">Jim Fanning</a>. The team continued to struggle, though, and had a 19\xe2\x80\x9319 record with 15 games left to play.<sup id="cite_ref-47" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-47">&#91;47&#93;</a></sup> Montreal won 11 of the remaining games and finished in first place, a 1/2 game ahead of the Pittsburgh Pirates, thereby qualifying for the franchise\'s first post-season berth.<sup id="cite_ref-Keri168_48-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Keri168-48">&#91;48&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-49" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-49">&#91;49&#93;</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Terry_Francona" title="Terry Francona">Terry Francona</a> caught the final out \xe2\x80\x93 a fly ball hit by <a href="/wiki/Dave_Kingman" title="Dave Kingman">Dave Kingman</a> \xe2\x80\x93 to seal a 5\xe2\x80\x934 victory over the New York Mets in the clinching game.<sup id="cite_ref-Keri168_48-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Keri168-48">&#91;48&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>In the <a href="/wiki/1981_National_League_Division_Series" title="1981 National League Division Series">1981 National League Division Series</a>, the Expos faced the first-half winners, the defending world champion Phillies.  Montreal won the first two games, at Olympic Stadium, by identical 3\xe2\x80\x931 scores before dropping the following two games in Philadelphia.  In the deciding fifth game, Montreal\'s Steve Rogers faced <a href="/wiki/Steve_Carlton" title="Steve Carlton">Steve Carlton</a> in a pitchers\' duel. Rogers pitched a complete-game shutout as Montreal advanced to the <a href="/wiki/1981_National_League_Championship_Series" title="1981 National League Championship Series">1981 National League Championship Series</a> with a 3\xe2\x80\x930 win.<sup id="cite_ref-50" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-50">&#91;50&#93;</a></sup> Facing the <a href="/wiki/Los_Angeles_Dodgers" title="Los Angeles Dodgers">Los Angeles Dodgers</a>, Montreal split the first two games of the best-of-five series in Los Angeles before returning home for the final three games. Montreal won game three, but failed in their first attempt to close out the series by losing game four and set up a deciding fifth game.<sup id="cite_ref-Keri173_51-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Keri173-51">&#91;51&#93;</a></sup> The deciding game, postponed by a day due to rain, was played October 19, 1981, in near-freezing temperatures.<sup id="cite_ref-52" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-52">&#91;52&#93;</a></sup> The game was tied at 1 entering the ninth inning when Fanning opted to have his top starter, Steve Rogers, come out of the <a href="/wiki/Bullpen" title="Bullpen">bullpen</a> to pitch.  Rogers retired the first two batters before facing <a href="/wiki/Rick_Monday" title="Rick Monday">Rick Monday</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-53" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-53">&#91;53&#93;</a></sup>  What followed was the defining moment in Expos history: on a 3\xe2\x80\x931 count, Rogers hung a <a href="/wiki/Sinker_(baseball)" title="Sinker (baseball)">sinking fastball</a> that Monday hit over the centrefield fence for the game-winning and series-clinching home run.<sup id="cite_ref-FailedDynasty_54-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FailedDynasty-54">&#91;54&#93;</a></sup> The moment, and game, became known to Expos fans as "Blue Monday".<sup id="cite_ref-55" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-55">&#91;55&#93;</a></sup> The dramatic loss was a bitter defeat for a franchise who by that time had been adopted as Canada\'s most popular baseball team.<sup id="cite_ref-56" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-56">&#91;56&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h3><span id=".22The_team_of_the_.2780s.22_.281982.E2.80.931988.29"></span><span class="mw-headline" id="&quot;The_team_of_the_\'80s&quot;_(1982\xe2\x80\x931988)">"The team of the \'80s" (1982\xe2\x80\x931988)</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Montreal_Expos&amp;action=edit&amp;section=5" title="Edit section: &quot;The team of the &#039;80s&quot; (1982\xe2\x80\x931988)">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Andres_galarraga2002.jpg" class="image"><img alt="Close-up view of Galarraga as he poses." src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/6c/Andres_galarraga2002.jpg/220px-Andres_galarraga2002.jpg" width="220" height="203" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/6c/Andres_galarraga2002.jpg/330px-Andres_galarraga2002.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/6c/Andres_galarraga2002.jpg/440px-Andres_galarraga2002.jpg 2x" data-file-width="1028" data-file-height="948" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Andres_galarraga2002.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div><a href="/wiki/Andr%C3%A9s_Galarraga" title="Andr\xc3\xa9s Galarraga">Andr\xc3\xa9s Galarraga</a>, pictured here in 2002, also played with the Expos from 1985 to 1991.</div></div></div>\n<p>By the end of the 1979 season, the Expos had earned a reputation for having one of the strongest player development systems in baseball; the team had stockpiled young talent throughout its roster including four starting pitchers below the age of 23, and was hailed as "the team of the \'80s".<sup id="cite_ref-FailedDynasty_54-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FailedDynasty-54">&#91;54&#93;</a></sup> When Montreal hosted the <a href="/wiki/1982_Major_League_Baseball_All-Star_Game" title="1982 Major League Baseball All-Star Game">1982 Major League Baseball All-Star Game</a> on July 13, 1982, Expos fans voted four of their own into the starting lineup: Carter, Dawson, Raines and Rogers, while <a href="/wiki/Al_Oliver" title="Al Oliver">Al Oliver</a> was named as a reserve.  It was only the second time since 1969 that the host team had four starters.<sup id="cite_ref-57" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-57">&#91;57&#93;</a></sup> The National League claimed a 4\xe2\x80\x931 victory in front of 59,057 fans in the first All-Star Game held outside of the United States; Rogers was the winning pitcher.<sup id="cite_ref-58" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-58">&#91;58&#93;</a></sup> Baseball historian and author <a href="/wiki/Jonah_Keri" title="Jonah Keri">Jonah Keri</a> argued in his book <i>Up, Up and Away</i> that  "no one at the stadium could know it then, but baseball in Montreal peaked that night at the Big O."<sup id="cite_ref-59" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-59">&#91;59&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>The Expos were widely predicted to win the NL East in <a href="/wiki/1982_Major_League_Baseball_season" title="1982 Major League Baseball season">1982</a>; <i><a href="/wiki/Sports_Illustrated" title="Sports Illustrated">Sports Illustrated</a></i>, <i><a href="/wiki/Baseball_Digest" title="Baseball Digest">Baseball Digest</a></i> and <i><a href="/wiki/The_Sporting_News" class="mw-redirect" title="The Sporting News">The Sporting News</a></i> were among the publications that favoured Montreal.<sup id="cite_ref-60" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-60">&#91;60&#93;</a></sup> However, the team disappointed. Montreal finished third in the division with 86 wins.<sup id="cite_ref-FailedDynasty_54-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FailedDynasty-54">&#91;54&#93;</a></sup> The Expos replaced Fanning with <a href="/wiki/Bill_Virdon" title="Bill Virdon">Bill Virdon</a> in <a href="/wiki/1983_in_baseball" title="1983 in baseball">1983</a>, and under their new manager, led the division in mid-July.<sup id="cite_ref-61" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-61">&#91;61&#93;</a></sup> However, the team faded down the stretch and finished with an 82\xe2\x80\x9380 record.<sup id="cite_ref-FailedDynasty_54-3" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FailedDynasty-54">&#91;54&#93;</a></sup> The Expos won more games between 1979 and 1983 than any other team in the NL East, but had only one postseason appearance to show for it.<sup id="cite_ref-62" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-62">&#91;62&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>Hoping to turn the team\'s fortunes around, the Expos signed 42-year-old veteran <a href="/wiki/Pete_Rose" title="Pete Rose">Pete Rose</a>, who was second all-time in base hits to <a href="/wiki/Ty_Cobb" title="Ty Cobb">Ty Cobb</a>, to a one-year contract in <a href="/wiki/1984_in_baseball" title="1984 in baseball">1984</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-63" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-63">&#91;63&#93;</a></sup> Rose reached a career milestone in Montreal\'s home opener by recording the 4,000th hit of his career in a 5\xe2\x80\x931 victory over Philadelphia on April 13.<sup id="cite_ref-64" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-64">&#91;64&#93;</a></sup> Though players and management had praised the acquisition of Rose and predicted he would help the team win the division, he was ineffective for Montreal.  Rose batted only .259 and failed to hit a home run in 95 games before he was traded back to his original team, Cincinnati,<sup id="cite_ref-65" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-65">&#91;65&#93;</a></sup> and Montreal finished with a losing record on the season.<sup id="cite_ref-FailedDynasty_54-4" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FailedDynasty-54">&#91;54&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>Montreal\'s failed 1984 season resulted in a 31 percent decrease in attendance at the same time salaries were escalating throughout baseball.<sup id="cite_ref-Keri_206_66-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Keri_206-66">&#91;66&#93;</a></sup> As a consequence, the Expos completed a major trade following the season, sending Gary Carter to the New York Mets on December 10, 1984, in exchange for four players.<sup id="cite_ref-67" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-67">&#91;67&#93;</a></sup> In trading Carter, the Expos gave up a team icon who, like Rusty Staub before him, endeared himself to the fans by learning French and being one of the most accessible players on the team.<sup id="cite_ref-Keri_206_66-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Keri_206-66">&#91;66&#93;</a></sup> The trade came one year after Bronfman had called the seven-year, US$12.6 million contract Carter signed in 1981 "the biggest mistake he had made in his life".<sup id="cite_ref-68" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-68">&#91;68&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>The economics of Major League Baseball also resulted in the departure of Andre Dawson following the <a href="/wiki/1986_in_baseball" title="1986 in baseball">1986</a> season. Throughout that off-season, MLB owners <a href="/wiki/Major_League_Baseball_collusion" title="Major League Baseball collusion">colluded</a> at the behest of Commissioner <a href="/wiki/Peter_Ueberroth" title="Peter Ueberroth">Peter Ueberroth</a> to drive salaries for free agents down.  Dawson, who should have been one of the most valuable <a href="/wiki/Free_agent" title="Free agent">free agents</a> on the market that year, discovered that not only was there little interest in signing him, but that the Expos were publicly commenting about his knee problems in an effort to further drive interest down.<sup id="cite_ref-69" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-69">&#91;69&#93;</a></sup> Angered by these actions, Dawson walked into the <a href="/wiki/Chicago_Cubs" title="Chicago Cubs">Chicago Cubs</a>\' training camp with a signed, blank contract. The Cubs agreed to sign Dawson to a one-year, $500,000 contract, less than half of his previous salary.<sup id="cite_ref-Tribune-GreenDawson_70-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Tribune-GreenDawson-70">&#91;70&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-BR-Dawson_71-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-BR-Dawson-71">&#91;71&#93;</a></sup>\nDawson hit 49 home runs and drove in 137 runs in <a href="/wiki/1987_in_baseball" title="1987 in baseball">1987</a>, attaining the honour of NL Most Valuable Player.<sup id="cite_ref-Keri222_72-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Keri222-72">&#91;72&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>Tim Raines was also affected by collusion: after receiving no offer worth more than the $1.5 million he earned in 1986, Raines returned to the Expos on a three-year, $5 million contract.<sup id="cite_ref-Keri222_72-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Keri222-72">&#91;72&#93;</a></sup> He had one of the best seasons of his career in 1987, leading the NL with 123 runs (in 139 games), stealing 50 bases, batting .330 and hitting 18 home runs.<sup id="cite_ref-73" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-73">&#91;73&#93;</a></sup> He was also named the most valuable player of the <a href="/wiki/1987_Major_League_Baseball_All-Star_Game" title="1987 Major League Baseball All-Star Game">1987 Major League Baseball All-Star Game</a>, as he drove in the game\'s only two runs with a triple in the 13th inning.<sup id="cite_ref-74" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-74">&#91;74&#93;</a></sup>  Raines was ultimately traded to the <a href="/wiki/Chicago_White_Sox" title="Chicago White Sox">Chicago White Sox</a> in 1990.<sup id="cite_ref-Humber124_75-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Humber124-75">&#91;75&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h3><span id=".22El_Presidente.2C_El_Perfecto.21.22_.281989.E2.80.931993.29"></span><span class="mw-headline" id="&quot;El_Presidente,_El_Perfecto!&quot;_(1989\xe2\x80\x931993)">"El Presidente, El Perfecto!" (1989\xe2\x80\x931993)</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Montreal_Expos&amp;action=edit&amp;section=6" title="Edit section: &quot;El Presidente, El Perfecto!&quot; (1989\xe2\x80\x931993)">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<div class="thumb tleft"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Expos1992.jpg" class="image"><img alt="A St. Louis runner breaks from first base as the Expos pitcher throws to the plate." src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/9/98/Expos1992.jpg/220px-Expos1992.jpg" width="220" height="180" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/9/98/Expos1992.jpg/330px-Expos1992.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/9/98/Expos1992.jpg/440px-Expos1992.jpg 2x" data-file-width="864" data-file-height="708" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Expos1992.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>The Expos, wearing their blue road uniforms, face the <a href="/wiki/St._Louis_Cardinals" title="St. Louis Cardinals">St. Louis Cardinals</a> in 1991</div></div></div>\n<p>On the field, the Expos won just four games more than they lost between 1986 and 1991 as the organization set about rebuilding its development system and acquiring a new generation of players.<sup id="cite_ref-76" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-76">&#91;76&#93;</a></sup> The team struggled to attract free agents to Montreal,<sup id="cite_ref-77" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-77">&#91;77&#93;</a></sup> and Bronfman had grown disillusioned with both the business of baseball and the challenge of drawing fans to Olympic Stadium for a middling ball club.<sup id="cite_ref-Keri236_78-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Keri236-78">&#91;78&#93;</a></sup> He hoped to take one more chance at winning a title, however, and in <a href="/wiki/1989_in_baseball" title="1989 in baseball">1989</a>, the Expos made a push for a division title by acquiring start pitcher and pending free agent <a href="/wiki/Mark_Langston" title="Mark Langston">Mark Langston</a> from the <a href="/wiki/Seattle_Mariners" title="Seattle Mariners">Seattle Mariners</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-Keri236_78-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Keri236-78">&#91;78&#93;</a></sup>  The price would ultimately prove to be a high one as the Expos gave up future Hall of Famer <a href="/wiki/Randy_Johnson" title="Randy Johnson">Randy Johnson</a> and two other pitchers.<sup id="cite_ref-JohnsonMartinezRetrospective_79-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-JohnsonMartinezRetrospective-79">&#91;79&#93;</a></sup> The trade helped propel the Expos to first place in the NL East by the All-Star break. They held the top spot into August before Langston and the team collapsed.<sup id="cite_ref-80" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-80">&#91;80&#93;</a></sup>  The Expos finished fourth in the division with an 81\xe2\x80\x9381 record,<sup id="cite_ref-81" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-81">&#91;81&#93;</a></sup> and Langston left Montreal as a free agent.<sup id="cite_ref-82" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-82">&#91;82&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>Bronfman grew increasingly uneasy about the reckless spending of his fellow team owners, increased strife with the players, and overall direction of MLB.<sup id="cite_ref-83" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-83">&#91;83&#93;</a></sup> According to then-team president <a href="/wiki/Claude_Brochu" title="Claude Brochu">Claude Brochu</a>, the team\'s late-season decline in 1989 proved too much for Bronfman, who asked him to seek a buyer for the team.<sup id="cite_ref-84" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-84">&#91;84&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>Bronfman hoped to sell the team for around $50 million, but both he and Brochu found it impossible to find a local businessman willing to take primary ownership of the team.<sup id="cite_ref-Keri236_78-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Keri236-78">&#91;78&#93;</a></sup>  Groups from American cities were interested, however.  One group offered to buy the club for $135 million and relocate it to Miami; however, Bronfman viewed a relocation as a last resort.<sup id="cite_ref-85" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-85">&#91;85&#93;</a></sup> Instead, Brochu opted to lead a group himself.  The city and the province agreed to fund $33 million of the $100 million sales price Bronfman had settled on,<sup id="cite_ref-86" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-86">&#91;86&#93;</a></sup> after which he and partner Jacques M\xc3\xa9nard convinced 11 other Canadian businesses and businessmen\xe2\x80\x94such as <a href="/wiki/Bell_Canada" title="Bell Canada">Bell Canada</a>, <a href="/wiki/Desjardins_Group" title="Desjardins Group">Desjardins Group</a>, the <a href="/wiki/Jean_Coutu_Group" title="Jean Coutu Group">Jean Coutu Group</a> and <a href="/wiki/Loblaw_Companies" title="Loblaw Companies">Loblaw Companies</a>\xe2\x80\x94to buy minority stakes.  The sale was completed on November 29, 1990.<sup id="cite_ref-87" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-87">&#91;87&#93;</a></sup> However, many of the investors Brochu cajoled into joining the partnership made it clear that they considered their investments to be the equivalent of charitable donations, and were not interested in providing additional funding.<sup id="cite_ref-88" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-88">&#91;88&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>With a new ownership group in place, the Expos traded Tim Raines to the <a href="/wiki/Chicago_White_Sox" title="Chicago White Sox">Chicago White Sox</a> in a five-player deal.<sup id="cite_ref-Raines-stats_89-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Raines-stats-89">&#91;89&#93;</a></sup>\nGeneral manager <a href="/wiki/David_Dombrowski" class="mw-redirect" title="David Dombrowski">David Dombrowski</a> fired manager <a href="/wiki/Buck_Rodgers" title="Buck Rodgers">Buck Rodgers</a>, who had managed the team since 1985, after the team started the 1991 season with a 20\xe2\x80\x9329 record,<sup id="cite_ref-90" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-90">&#91;90&#93;</a></sup> replacing him with <a href="/wiki/Tom_Runnells" title="Tom Runnells">Tom Runnells</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-91" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-91">&#91;91&#93;</a></sup>\n<a href="/wiki/Mark_Gardner_(baseball)" title="Mark Gardner (baseball)">Mark Gardner</a> pitched nine no-hit innings in a July 26, <a href="/wiki/1991_in_baseball" title="1991 in baseball">1991</a> game before losing 1\xe2\x80\x930 in the 10th inning to the Los Angeles Dodgers.<sup id="cite_ref-92" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-92">&#91;92&#93;</a></sup>  Two days later, also in Los Angeles, <a href="/wiki/Dennis_Mart%C3%ADnez" title="Dennis Mart\xc3\xadnez">Dennis Mart\xc3\xadnez</a> achieved a rare feat, throwing the <a href="/wiki/Dennis_Mart%C3%ADnez%27s_perfect_game" title="Dennis Mart\xc3\xadnez&#39;s perfect game">13th official perfect game</a> in Major League Baseball history (based on MLB\'s 1991 redefinition of a <a href="/wiki/Perfect_game" title="Perfect game">perfect game</a>), winning 2\xe2\x80\x930.<sup id="cite_ref-MartinezPerfectGame_93-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-MartinezPerfectGame-93">&#91;93&#93;</a></sup> Dave Van Horne\'s iconic call of "El Presidente, El Perfecto!" following the final out became a hallmark of Expos lore.<sup id="cite_ref-94" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-94">&#91;94&#93;</a></sup> Martinez\'s catcher, <a href="/wiki/Ron_Hassey" title="Ron Hassey">Ron Hassey</a>, also caught <a href="/wiki/Len_Barker%27s_perfect_game" title="Len Barker&#39;s perfect game">Len Barker\'s perfect game</a> ten years earlier and remains the only player to catch two perfect games in MLB history.<sup id="cite_ref-95" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-95">&#91;95&#93;</a></sup> The euphoria of the pitching feats did not last, as the Expos were rendered homeless for the final month of the season after a 50-ton beam collapsed from Olympic Stadium\'s structure and fell nine metres onto a public concourse hours before a <a href="/wiki/Motocross" title="Motocross">motocross</a> event on September 13.<sup id="cite_ref-96" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-96">&#91;96&#93;</a></sup>  The Expos hinted that they would have to open the 1992 season elsewhere unless Olympic Stadium was certified safe.  While the stadium itself was given a clean bill of health by engineers in November, it took longer to get one for the roof since it had been badly ripped in a June windstorm.  Ultimately, it was decided to keep the roof closed at all times; it had only been opened 88 times in a little more than four years.<sup id="cite_ref-SABROlympicStadium_31-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-SABROlympicStadium-31">&#91;31&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>The Expos finished 1991 with a 71\xe2\x80\x9390 record, sixth in the NL East, and drew fewer than one million fans for the first time since 1976.<sup id="cite_ref-2004MG6_97-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-2004MG6-97">&#91;97&#93;</a></sup> However, the foundation of the Expos\' future was establishing their places in MLB:  <a href="/wiki/Larry_Walker" title="Larry Walker">Larry Walker</a>, <a href="/wiki/Marquis_Grissom" title="Marquis Grissom">Marquis Grissom</a> and <a href="/wiki/Delino_DeShields" title="Delino DeShields">Delino DeShields</a> had made their debuts the season prior,<sup id="cite_ref-98" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-98">&#91;98&#93;</a></sup> and the team acquired <a href="/wiki/Mois%C3%A9s_Alou" title="Mois\xc3\xa9s Alou">Mois\xc3\xa9s Alou</a> in a trade with Pittsburgh.<sup id="cite_ref-99" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-99">&#91;99&#93;</a></sup> Moises\' father <a href="/wiki/Felipe_Alou" title="Felipe Alou">Felipe</a>, who had been a long time employee of the Expos, was promoted to manager during the <a href="/wiki/1992_Major_League_Baseball_season" title="1992 Major League Baseball season">1992</a> season and became the first native of the Dominican Republic to manage a Major League Baseball team.<sup id="cite_ref-100" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-100">&#91;100&#93;</a></sup> In <a href="/wiki/1993_Major_League_Baseball_season" title="1993 Major League Baseball season">1993</a>, DeShields was sent to Los Angeles in exchange for <a href="/wiki/Pedro_Mart%C3%ADnez" title="Pedro Mart\xc3\xadnez">Pedro Mart\xc3\xadnez</a>; the deal was initially pilloried by the <i><a href="/wiki/Montreal_Gazette" title="Montreal Gazette">Montreal Gazette</a></i> and other local publications as a move designed to save money rather than improve the ball club.<sup id="cite_ref-JohnsonMartinezRetrospective_79-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-JohnsonMartinezRetrospective-79">&#91;79&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-101" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-101">&#91;101&#93;</a></sup>  Nonetheless, the Expos improved on the field; they won 87 games in 1992, 94 in 1993 and finished second in the NL East both seasons.<sup id="cite_ref-2004MG6_97-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-2004MG6-97">&#91;97&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h3><span id="1994_and_the_players.27_strike"></span><span class="mw-headline" id="1994_and_the_players\'_strike">1994 and the players\' strike</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Montreal_Expos&amp;action=edit&amp;section=7" title="Edit section: 1994 and the players&#039; strike">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<div class="quotebox pullquote floatright" style="width:30%;&#32;;"><style data-mw-deduplicate="TemplateStyles:r856303512">.mw-parser-output .quotebox{background-color:#F9F9F9;border:1px solid #aaa;box-sizing:border-box;padding:10px;font-size:88%}.mw-parser-output .quotebox.floatleft{margin:0.5em 1.4em 0.8em 0}.mw-parser-output .quotebox.floatright{margin:0.5em 0 0.8em 1.4em}.mw-parser-output .quotebox.centered{margin:0.5em auto 0.8em auto}.mw-parser-output .quotebox.floatleft p,.mw-parser-output .quotebox.floatright p{font-style:inherit}.mw-parser-output .quotebox-title{background-color:#F9F9F9;text-align:center;font-size:larger;font-weight:bold}.mw-parser-output .quotebox-quote.quoted:before{font-family:"Times New Roman",serif;font-weight:bold;font-size:large;color:gray;content:" \xe2\x80\x9c ";vertical-align:-45%;line-height:0}.mw-parser-output .quotebox-quote.quoted:after{font-family:"Times New Roman",serif;font-weight:bold;font-size:large;color:gray;content:" \xe2\x80\x9d ";line-height:0}.mw-parser-output .quotebox .left-aligned{text-align:left}.mw-parser-output .quotebox .right-aligned{text-align:right}.mw-parser-output .quotebox .center-aligned{text-align:center}.mw-parser-output .quotebox cite{display:block;font-style:normal}@media screen and (max-width:360px){.mw-parser-output .quotebox{min-width:100%;margin:0 0 0.8em!important;float:none!important}}</style>\n<div class="quotebox-quote left-aligned" style="">"Most of my career, you\'d go to the park that night, and hope you were going to win it. In \'94, we pretty much knew were going to win it. Losing wasn\'t part of the equation. After the [All-Star] break, we played the Braves and beat \'em again. I remember leaving Atlanta, and we were just laughing. Like, \'This is our competition?!\'"</div>\n<p><cite class="left-aligned" style="">\xe2\x80\x94Larry Walker\'s retrospective of the 1994 Expos.<sup id="cite_ref-Keri307_102-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Keri307-102">&#91;102&#93;</a></sup></cite>\n</p>\n</div>\n<p>The Expos were recognized as having a strong team entering the <a href="/wiki/1994_Major_League_Baseball_season" title="1994 Major League Baseball season">1994</a> season, but their hopes of winning the division were significantly impacted by realignment, as the National League\'s most dominant team, the <a href="/wiki/Atlanta_Braves" title="Atlanta Braves">Atlanta Braves</a>, were shifted from the West to the East.<sup id="cite_ref-103" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-103">&#91;103&#93;</a></sup> Atlanta opened the season with 13 wins in 14 games, and quickly opened up an 8 1/2 game lead on Montreal.<sup id="cite_ref-104" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-104">&#91;104&#93;</a></sup> By late June, the Expos had moved to 2 1/2 games back when they hosted the Braves.  Montreal won two out of three games in the series, including a late-game victory in the opener over future Hall of Fame pitcher <a href="/wiki/Greg_Maddux" title="Greg Maddux">Greg Maddux</a> that the players viewed as the turning point of their season.<sup id="cite_ref-105" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-105">&#91;105&#93;</a></sup> Montreal then embarked on a west coast road trip in which they won the final five games and entered the All-Star break in first place.<sup id="cite_ref-106" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-106">&#91;106&#93;</a></sup> The Expos pulled away from the Braves after the break; between July 18 and August 11, Montreal won 20 games and lost only three.<sup id="cite_ref-Keri307_102-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Keri307-102">&#91;102&#93;</a></sup> For the second time in team history, five players were named all-stars: <a href="/wiki/Mois%C3%A9s_Alou" title="Mois\xc3\xa9s Alou">Mois\xc3\xa9s Alou</a>, <a href="/wiki/Wil_Cordero" title="Wil Cordero">Wil Cordero</a>,  <a href="/wiki/Darrin_Fletcher" title="Darrin Fletcher">Darrin Fletcher</a>, <a href="/wiki/Marquis_Grissom" title="Marquis Grissom">Marquis Grissom</a> and <a href="/wiki/Ken_Hill_(baseball)" title="Ken Hill (baseball)">Ken Hill</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-107" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-107">&#91;107&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>With a record of 74\xe2\x80\x9340, the Expos had the best record in baseball on the morning of August 12, when MLB\'s players <a href="/wiki/1994%E2%80%9395_Major_League_Baseball_strike" title="1994\xe2\x80\x9395 Major League Baseball strike">went on strike</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-108" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-108">&#91;108&#93;</a></sup> The season began without a collective bargaining agreement as MLB\'s owners could not agree on how to share revenue between teams.  Many teams were unwilling to agree to revenue sharing unless a <a href="/wiki/Salary_cap" title="Salary cap">salary cap</a> was put in place, something which the <a href="/wiki/Major_League_Baseball_Players%27_Association" class="mw-redirect" title="Major League Baseball Players&#39; Association">Major League Baseball Players\' Association</a> (MLBPA) adamantly opposed. Unable to come to an agreement, the owners attempted to unilaterally force their system into effect, prompting the players to walk out.  Most of the players believed they would be back on the field by the American Labor Day at the latest.<sup id="cite_ref-109" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-109">&#91;109&#93;</a></sup> On September 14, following a month of fruitless negotiations, the remainder of the season was cancelled.<sup id="cite_ref-110" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-110">&#91;110&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>From Brochu\'s perspective, a salary cap was not a major concern for the Expos as they could not afford to spend the maximum value of any negotiated cap. But when the strike ended eight months later, by the order of United States federal judge <a href="/wiki/Sonia_Sotomayor" title="Sonia Sotomayor">Sonia Sotomayor</a>, the failure to implement strong revenue sharing was a major blow to the Expos.<sup id="cite_ref-111" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-111">&#91;111&#93;</a></sup> The team had already built a reputation as a penny-pinching organization (Larry Walker once complained in the media that the team asked the players to buy their own vitamins),<sup id="cite_ref-112" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-112">&#91;112&#93;</a></sup> with the second-lowest payroll in MLB in 1994.<sup id="cite_ref-113" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-113">&#91;113&#93;</a></sup> Following the strike, the team initiated a <a href="/wiki/Fire_sale" title="Fire sale">fire sale</a> of players: <a href="/wiki/Ken_Hill_(baseball)" title="Ken Hill (baseball)">Ken Hill</a>, <a href="/wiki/John_Wetteland" title="John Wetteland">John Wetteland</a> and Marquis Grissom were traded while Larry Walker was allowed to leave as a free agent. Mois\xc3\xa9s Alou, Pedro Mart\xc3\xadnez and <a href="/wiki/Mel_Rojas" title="Mel Rojas">Mel Rojas</a> would eventually follow.<sup id="cite_ref-CBS1994Retrospective_114-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-CBS1994Retrospective-114">&#91;114&#93;</a></sup> In his book, <i>My Turn At Bat</i>, Brochu argued that the fire sale was the only viable option, since his partners in the ownership group were not interested in financing the team\'s losses. Brochu estimated that had he tried to keep the 1994 team together, the Expos would have lost $25 million in 1995, which would have pushed the franchise to the edge of bankruptcy.  He claimed that he would have certainly kept Hill, Wetteland, Grissom and Walker had the partners been willing to put up the money necessary to keep them in Montreal.<sup id="cite_ref-115" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-115">&#91;115&#93;</a></sup>  When Brochu told general manager <a href="/wiki/Kevin_Malone_(baseball)" title="Kevin Malone (baseball)">Kevin Malone</a> that Hill, Wetteland, Grissom and Walker all had to go, Malone tried to persuade Brochu to keep at least one of them.  It was to no avail; Brochu told Malone that they all had to be off the roster by the deadline for salary arbitration\xe2\x80\x94even though this made it all but impossible to get any leverage in possible deals.  As a result, the Expos got almost nothing in return.<sup id="cite_ref-116" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-116">&#91;116&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h3><span id="Decline_.281995.E2.80.932000.29"></span><span class="mw-headline" id="Decline_(1995\xe2\x80\x932000)">Decline (1995\xe2\x80\x932000)</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Montreal_Expos&amp;action=edit&amp;section=8" title="Edit section: Decline (1995\xe2\x80\x932000)">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<p>The strike and ensuing fire sale left fans in Montreal livid.<sup id="cite_ref-117" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-117">&#91;117&#93;</a></sup> The Expos finished last in the NL East in <a href="/wiki/1995_Major_League_Baseball_season" title="1995 Major League Baseball season">1995</a>, and average game attendance fell by nearly 26%, from 24,543 to 18,189.  Interest in the Expos continued to decline in the years that followed;<sup id="cite_ref-CBS1994Retrospective_114-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-CBS1994Retrospective-114">&#91;114&#93;</a></sup> they would never average more than 20,000 fans per game in a season again during their tenure in Montreal.<sup id="cite_ref-TBT_118-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-TBT-118">&#91;118&#93;</a></sup> While noting the Atlanta Braves went on to win 11 consecutive NL East titles following the strike, <a href="/wiki/Jonah_Keri" title="Jonah Keri">Jonah Keri</a> expressed the viewpoint of the fans as it related to Brochu and the team\'s owners: "Expos fans couldn\'t help but wonder if that could have been <i>them</i> celebrating every year ... had Brochu convinced the team\'s cheapskate owners to spend a few damn dollars, or taken a leap of faith that short-term financial pain would lead to long-term success."<sup id="cite_ref-119" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-119">&#91;119&#93;</a></sup>  The media, meanwhile, had taken to calling the Expos a "Triple-A team" as the team seemed to enter a period where they would develop players only to move them on to other organizations.<sup id="cite_ref-120" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-120">&#91;120&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>In spite of a sharp decline in attendance, Brochu claimed the Expos turned a small profit in 1995. While ticket sales increased in other markets in the seasons following the strike, though, Montreal\'s fan base continued to erode.<sup id="cite_ref-121" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-121">&#91;121&#93;</a></sup> Even with the loss of most of their best players, the Expos were competitive in <a href="/wiki/1996_Major_League_Baseball_season" title="1996 Major League Baseball season">1996</a>, achieving second place in the NL East with an 88\xe2\x80\x9374 record. The team fared poorly in the following five seasons, however, finishing with a losing record in each year and no higher than fourth in the division.<sup id="cite_ref-2004MG6_97-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-2004MG6-97">&#91;97&#93;</a></sup> Individually, Pedro Mart\xc3\xadnez became the first native of the Dominican Republic\xe2\x80\x94and only Expo\xe2\x80\x94to win the National League <a href="/wiki/Cy_Young_Award" title="Cy Young Award">Cy Young Award</a>. He won the award in <a href="/wiki/1997_Major_League_Baseball_season" title="1997 Major League Baseball season">1997</a> after recording an 18\xe2\x80\x937 record with an <a href="/wiki/Earned_run_average" title="Earned run average">earned run average</a> (ERA) of 1.90.<sup id="cite_ref-122" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-122">&#91;122&#93;</a></sup> One week after he was announced as the NL Cy Young winner, Mart\xc3\xadnez was traded to the <a href="/wiki/Boston_Red_Sox" title="Boston Red Sox">Boston Red Sox</a> as part of another salary purge.<sup id="cite_ref-123" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-123">&#91;123&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>As the 1990s wore on, interest in the Expos dwindled to the point that they were barely part of Montreal\'s sports landscape.  Alou recalled in the latter part of the decade, an old friend of his who owned a team in the Dominican Republic came to Montreal for a visit and couldn\'t find any downtown store that sold Expos caps, nor did he see anyone wearing an Expos cap during his weeklong stay in the city.  When he took a taxi to a game at Olympic Stadium, the driver couldn\'t find the entrance, and there were no signs anywhere touting games.  According to Alou\'s friend, with such lackluster marketing, it was no surprise that the Expos couldn\'t attract any fans.<sup id="cite_ref-124" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-124">&#91;124&#93;</a></sup>  Keri later wrote that the Expos would not have been in this position had a better-financed "champion" with the resources and the patience to shepherd the team through the 1990s bought the team.<sup id="cite_ref-125" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-125">&#91;125&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>Brochu attempted to convince his partners that the only long-term solution to keep the Expos in Montreal was to replace Olympic Stadium. In addition to being poorly located\xe2\x80\x94far from population centres, restaurants, and bars\xe2\x80\x94fans perceived it as cavernous and unsafe. Additionally, free agents were letting it be known they were not willing to play for the Expos because of Olympic Stadium\'s poor playing conditions.<sup id="cite_ref-126" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-126">&#91;126&#93;</a></sup> A proposed 35,000-seat downtown facility, to be called Labatt Park, was announced in 1997 with a budgeted cost of $250 million and an anticipated opening date of 2001.  It would have been a retro-classic park with a facade reminiscent of historic <a href="/wiki/Bonaventure_Station_(1887%E2%80%931952)" title="Bonaventure Station (1887\xe2\x80\x931952)">Bonaventure Station</a>.  According to a <a href="/wiki/Montreal_Gazette" title="Montreal Gazette">Montreal Gazette</a> editorial supporting the new park, Brochu\'s threat to move the team unless Olympic Stadium was replaced was "simple logic."
